<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">This paper at first illustrates implementation aspects and measurement results of a subcomponent for a multistandard RF identification (RFID) transponder. It is intended to be a common reference cell, both for basic UHF requirements and advanced application fields like local positioning and wireless sensing. Different single circuit topologies shown in previous studies or literature and their applicability for that RFID system are evaluated. After that, measurement results of two final circuit configurations, including a newly designed RC oscillator with metal-metal capacitors, are discussed and compared. Layout aspects for reducing the process variations and low power consumption are demonstrated. Simulation results show border conditions for the power supply of the transponder on chip level. Moreover, distance measurements with our first complete transponder compliant to the electronic product code protocol are shown. It includes the newly presented reference cells and other necessary transponder components. All chips are designed based on a 0.13-Î¼m CMOS technology.</div>

						<!-- ngIf: ::vm.fullTextAccess --><a ng-click="vm.scrollTo(item.id,item.part,'toc-link')" ng-if="::vm.fullTextAccess" class="ng-binding ng-scope">VI.Â Conclusion and Outlook</a><!-- end ngIf: ::vm.fullTextAccess -->
						<!-- ngIf: ::!vm.fullTextAccess -->
						<section class="pure-u-1-1">

Various sensor systems like odometry, INS, ultra sonic, laser lange finder (LRF), RF range systems such as UWB and chirp spread-spectrum (CSS), and vision have been applied to solve localization problem. RFID system can be a solution due to the low cost and scalability. A RFID system used to localize mobile robot in distributed tags on the floor is called RFID Tag floor localization system. font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/238/0054.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 8px; margin-right: -0.117em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-5">V_{T}</script></tex-math></inline-formula></td><td><p>Thermal voltage.</p></td></tr></tbody></table><p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>RF Indentification (RFID) is an umbrella term for many individual auto-identification (auto-ID) technologies with significantly different parameters and properties depending on the concrete application <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>. It does not only denote radio technology, but also includes several other technical areas. A reliable institutional framework is very important so that the products and developments of different manufacturers work together. Besides that, frequency bands are a very limited resource in which different communication systems have to coexist without disturbing each other.</p><p>Due to this fact, RFID systems are only allowed to use frequency ranges that are reserved for industrial, scientific, and medical (ISM) applications (ISM bands) or especially for RFID <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>. Therefore, standardization of RFID systems aims for those exclusive spectra. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1</a> provides an overview on frequency bands usable for RFID. Several spectra are restricted to a certain region. The actual allowed bandwidth and the maximum power within these frequency ranges are restricted by several national or regional regulations, e.g., <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>â<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>. Standards regarding RFID must include frequencies, communication, data, networks, safety, and applications. Moreover, an international coordination must be performed. In that area, it is distinguished between industrial and institutional standards. The former are oriented toward the interests and requirements of the industry, and their adoption is generally not mandatory. Here, the company EPCglobal is the most important nonprofit organization that develops the electronic product code (EPC) standard (RFID air interface) as a successor of the conventional barcode. The standard EPC Class 1 Gen2 UHF is intended for the UHF region <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a>. EPC Gen2 HF for the HF region was developed based on EPC UHF <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a>. The (institutional) ISO standard 18000-6c <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a> is in conformance with the EPC Class1 Gen2 standard. For a basic introduction to RFID, refer to <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_1">[10]</a>, and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_1">[11]</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 1. </b><fig><p>Available worldwide frequency bands for RFID.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5688469/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>Besides completely passive transponders, which are only powered by the RF field of RFID readers, EPC UHF also specifies tags with their own power supply only for sensors (EPC Class 3, semiactive) or for all (EPC Class 4, active) functionalities. A similiar standard exists for the microwave range of 2.45 GHz <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_1">[12]</a>. Higher frequency ranges are also approved for RFID, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1</a>, but to the knowledge of the authors, these bands are rarely used at the moment.</p><p>The higher operating range of UHF RFID systems in the far field enables the implementation of additional features like distance measurement between RFID reader and transponder <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_1">[13]</a>â<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_1">[14]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_1">[15]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_1">[16]</a> or wireless sensing <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref17" id="context_ref_17_1">[17]</a>â<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref18" id="context_ref_18_1">[18]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref19" id="context_ref_19_1">[19]</a>. Nevertheless, the functionality of more complex features implemented in passive transponders are still limited by free-air loss. By using active transponders, the operating range can still be extended. EPC offers the possibility to implement such functionalities with <i>custom commands</i> into the protocol. A related custom command only initiates a user-defined function compliant to the protocol. Its content is not part of the standard and can be set freely by the manufacturer.</p><p>The hardware design of the RFID reader is typically relaxed using lumped components and packaged chips on a printed circuit board (PCB). In contrast to that, all components of the transponder must be concentrated on a single chip. They are connected to their antenna directly or via the matching circuit <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref20" id="context_ref_20_1">[20]</a>. Designing a passive tag is most desirable because no additional supply voltage is needed that may introduce further problems (e.g., bad contact to battery or the need for battery changee). Besides different, more severe aspects of circuit design, as described in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref20" id="context_ref_20_1">[20]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref21" id="context_ref_21_1">[21]</a>, passive UHF transponders offer only a very limited power of some microwatts and a supply voltage of typically 1.0â1.5 V. Furthermore, they must also tolerate high power levels when they are very close to the reader. With the restricted possible power consumption and the related supply voltage as the challenging design constraints for a passive transponder, it must be cut back on other performance considerations. The situation becomes more complicated if several new features should be used together in one transponder. Power consumption can be reduced by device scaling. The power consumption of a digital gate is proportional to the square of the supply voltage <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">({VDD})^{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-6-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-29" role="math" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-30" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-31" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0028.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 5px; height: 16px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-32" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-33" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-34" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0056.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 12px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: -0.177em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.183em;"></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-35" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0044.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 13px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-36" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0044.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 13px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-37" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.784em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.3em 4.447em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-38" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0029.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 5px; height: 16px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 0.363em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-39" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-40" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-41" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0032.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 5px; height: 8px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-6">({VDD})^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref22" id="context_ref_22_1">[22]</a>. However, this leads to a reduction of electrical quantities, which can degrade the device performance.</p><p>This paper is organized as follows. In <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2" class="fulltext-link">SectionÂ II</a>, the treated RFID scenario is introduced. The integration of the newly designed reference cells into the whole transponder is explained on block-level and the necessary requirements for these subcomponents are discussed. In <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">SectionÂ III</a>, different circuit architectures that could be used for these reference cells are evaluated and compared. In <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4" class="fulltext-link">SectionÂ IV</a>, measurement results of the two newly designed subcomponents are illustrated. In <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec5a" class="fulltext-link">SectionsÂ V-A</a> and <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec5b" class="fulltext-link">B</a>, simulation results regarding power supply and modulated backscattering with passive tags are shown, and finally, in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec5c" class="fulltext-link">SectionÂ V-C</a>, measurement results with our first transponder consisting of the complete transponder chip and a custom-made transponder antenna are presented.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>System Overview</h2></div><p>The chip design for the transponder shall be evaluated first without a certain antenna architecture. According to <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref23" id="context_ref_23_2">[23]</a>, an arbitrary antenna structure can be represented by its equivalent circuit. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 2</a> shows the block diagram of the transponder antenna and the analog frontend. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{\rm Loss}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-7-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-42" role="math" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-43" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-44" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.045em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-45" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0052.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 11px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-46" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-47" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-48" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/004C.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 8px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-49" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/006F.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 5px; height: 5px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-50" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0073.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 4px; height: 5px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-51" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0073.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 4px; height: 5px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-7">R_{\rm Loss}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> describes the resistive losses of the antenna (here assumed 5 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Omega</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-8-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-52" role="math" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-53" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-54" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/03A9.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 11px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-8">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for simulation). <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">X_{\rm Ant}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-9-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-55" role="math" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-56" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-57" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.985em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-58" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0058.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 13px; height: 11px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-59" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-60" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-61" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0041.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 8px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-62" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/006E.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 6px; height: 5px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-63" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0074.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 4px; height: 7px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-9">X_{\rm Ant}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> equals the radiation impedance. It is only a fictitious impedance that represents the conversion of the wire-bound energy to the radiated one. The fixture describes the parasitic effects of the transponder setup, such as the pad capacitance of the chip, the inductance of the bond wire, and resistive losses of the stripline between the antenna and chip. The matching circuit usually realized by passive lumped components must achieve a power matching of the antenna impedance to the chip impedance including the fixture.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig2"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-2-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 2. </b><fig><p>Transponder antenna and analog frontend.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5688469/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>All presented circuits are designed with respect to the EPC protocol. According to it, amplitude shift-keying (ASK) and/or phase-shift keying (PSK) modulation can be used by the backscatter modulator for data communication from the UHF transponder back to the UHF reader <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_2">[7]</a>. The respective modulation technique can be realized using different combinations of lumped components <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_2">[11]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref24" id="context_ref_24_2">[24]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref25" id="context_ref_25_2">[25]</a>. In general PSK modulation is more efficient than ASK modulation because the available power is almost constant at both modulation states <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref26" id="context_ref_26_2">[26]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref27" id="context_ref_27_2">[27]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref28" id="context_ref_28_2">[28]</a>.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 3</a> demonstrates the switching of the backscatter modulator between its two common modulation states. The impedances <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">X_{1}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-10-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-64" role="math" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-65" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-66" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-67" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0058.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 13px; height: 11px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-68" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-69" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-70" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0031.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 5px; height: 8px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-10">X_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">X_{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-11-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-71" role="math" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-72" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-73" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-74" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0058.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 13px; height: 11px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-75" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-76" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-77" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0032.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 5px; height: 8px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-11">X_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are mostly realized by resistors or capacitors. In this approach, a shunt transistor in front of the rectifier circuit was used as the backscatter modulator, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 2</a>. It mainly performs a resistive modulation between the on and off resistance of the transistor enabling a mixture of ASK and PSK modulation for the UHF transponder <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref25" id="context_ref_25_2">[25]</a>. The load capacitance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{\rm Buffer}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-12-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-78" role="math" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-79" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-80" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.646em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-81" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0043.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 12px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-82" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-83" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-84" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0042.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 8px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-85" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0066.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 4px; height: 8px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-87" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0066.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 4px; height: 8px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-88" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0065.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 5px; height: 5px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-89" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0072.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 4px; height: 5px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-12">C_{\rm Buffer}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 2</a> at the output of the rectifier circuit is used for storing the rectified power of a passive transponder. It must guarantee that the chip can collect sufficient energy to stay operational during backscattering. This is usually performed by the oxide capacitance of MOS transistors. Since it is only used for storing energy, its nonlinear behavior is not of interest. The nonlinear load <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{L}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-13-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-90" role="math" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-91" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-92" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-93" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0052.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 11px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-94" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-95" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-96" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/238/004C.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 8px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-13">R_{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> represents the dc power consumption of all implemented transponder circuits.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig3"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-3-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 3. </b><fig><p>Common modulation states of UHF backscatter modulator.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5688469/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The third part of the analog frontend is the data recovery of the data sent by the reader. Design criteria and system topologies of the analog frontend are discussed in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_2">[11]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref20" id="context_ref_20_2">[20]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref24" id="context_ref_24_2">[24]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref25" id="context_ref_25_2">[25]</a>, and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref29" id="context_ref_29_2">[29]</a>â<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref30" id="context_ref_30_2">[30]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref31" id="context_ref_31_2">[31]</a>.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 4</a> shows the block diagram for the reference subcomponent. One would have the possibility to use the rectified voltage <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">VDD</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-14-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-97" role="math" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-17">I_{\rm Bias1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are used for biasing the regulator. Using a regulator stage improves the supply voltage and therefore the oscillator frequency, but the cost is a higher minimal supply voltage <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">VDD</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-18-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-135" role="math" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-136" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-137" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0056.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 12px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: -0.177em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.183em;"></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-138" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0044.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 13px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-139" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0044.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 13px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-18">VDD</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref32" id="context_ref_32_2">[32]</a>. A bias current <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">I_{\rm Bias2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-19-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-140" role="math" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-141" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-142" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.045em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.48em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-143" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0049.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 11px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; For wireless sensing, a reference voltage <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{\rm Ref,ADC}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-20-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-151" role="math" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0044.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 8px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-172" style="display: inline-block; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-21">f_{\rm ADC}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are necessary for an ADC <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref33" id="context_ref_33_2">[33]</a> in the transponder chip, which digitizes the sensing data of a sensor. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{\rm Ref,Sens}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-22-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-173" role="math" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-174" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-175" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.126em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-176" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0056.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 12px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: -0.177em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.183em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.544em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-177" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-178" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-179" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0052.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 8px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-180" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0065.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 5px; height: 5px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-181" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0066.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 4px; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/002C.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 2px; height: 4px; vertical-align: -2px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-183" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0053.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 6px; height: 8px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-184" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0065.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 5px; height: 5px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-185" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/006E.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 6px; height: 5px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-186" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0073.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 4px; height: 5px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-22">V_{\rm Ref,Sens}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is used for setting the operation point of the low-power temperature sensor. For the implementation of the used low-power ADC and the related wireless sensor circuit, which are not the subject of this paper, refer to <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref17" id="context_ref_17_2">[17]</a>â<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref18" id="context_ref_18_2">[18]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref19" id="context_ref_19_2">[19]</a>, and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref34" id="context_ref_34_2">[34]</a>. Furthermore, several bias currents are necessary for the components of the analog frontend.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-4-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 4. </b><fig><p>Multipurpose subcomponent.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5688469/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>Considering all these requirements, a common component is desired that can deliver both different bias currents and different reference voltages within reliable process characteristics.</p><p>A novel design trend is multistandard transponders, which support both UHF and HF readers with one common tag <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref33" id="context_ref_33_2">[33]</a>. This also causes further requirements for the transponder chip. According to the EPC protocol, UHF transponders have to implement their own tag oscillator <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_2">[7]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref33" id="context_ref_33_2">[33]</a>. Against that, HF transponders derive their clock signal from the RF signal of the high-frequency (HF) reader <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_2">[8]</a>. Therefore, a power switch is used to disable the reference oscillator in the HF mode by the control signal <i>Osc_OnOff</i> in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 4</a>. Actually there should be enough power in the HF mode so it would be sufficient only to disable the oscillator output signal <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{\rm Tag}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-23-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-187" role="math" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-188" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-189" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.54em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-190" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0066.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 14px; vertical-align: -3px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-191" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-192" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-193" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0054.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 8px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-194" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0061.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 6px; height: 5px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-195" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0067.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 5px; height: 7px; vertical-align: -2px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-23">f_{\rm Tag}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. However, shutting down the whole circuit would be useful when the transponder is part of a wireless sensor network, for example, and the HF communication is disabled for a certain time. In wireless sensor networks, only the memory cells with the acquired sensing data are supplied by an external battery supply. The data can be saved temporarily in the transponder until the next reading out of the related UHF reader (e.g., checking the compliance of the cold chain of food during transportation). The additional current consumption of the oscillator can be avoided and the lifetime of the battery is extended. The switch is also beneficial to enable a defined powering up. The oscillator is started when all analog circuit nodes are within their final operation points to perform a defined power up sequence.</p><p>The actual data rate for the data transfer from the transponder back to the reader is determined by several EPC parameters set by the reader via a <i>Query</i> command <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_2">[7]</a>. The backscatter-link frequency (BLF) is defined as <disp-formula id="deqn1" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm BLF}={{\rm DR}\over {\rm TRcal}} \eqno{\hbox{(1)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-24-Frame" tabindex="0" style="font-size: 111%;"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-24">{\rm BLF}={{\rm DR}\over {\rm TRcal}} \eqno{\hbox{(1)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">{\rm BLF}={{\rm DR}\over {\rm TRcal}} \eqno{\hbox{(1)}}</span></span></disp-formula>where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm DR}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-25-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-25">{\rm DR}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the divide ratio and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm TRcal}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-26-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-26">{\rm TRcal}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the tag-to-interrogator calibration symbol. BLF is in the range [40 kHz, 640 kHz]. While <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm DR}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-27-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-27">{\rm DR}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> has only two possible values <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">({\rm DR}=\{64/3,8\})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-28-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-28">({\rm DR}=\{64/3,8\})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm TRcal}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-29-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-29">{\rm TRcal}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can be set arbitrarily within a certain interval. It is in the range [33.3 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mu{\hbox {s}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-30-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-30">\mu{\hbox {s}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, 225 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mu{\hbox {s}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-31-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-31">\mu{\hbox {s}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>] for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm DR}=64/3</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-32-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-32">{\rm DR}=64/3</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and in the range [17.2 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mu{\hbox {s}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-33-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-33">\mu{\hbox {s}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, 200 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mu{\hbox {s}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-34-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-34">\mu{\hbox {s}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>] for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm DR}=8</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-35-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-35">{\rm DR}=8</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Finally, the parameter <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M=\{1;2;4;8\}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-36-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-36">M=\{1;2;4;8\}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> sets the modulation type (FM0 or Miller subcarrier). It determines the number of subcarrier cycles per symbol, and therefore the data rate (BLF/M).</p><p>A counter clocked by the reference oscillator of the transponder measures the duration of the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm TRcal}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-37-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-37">{\rm TRcal}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> interval, as illustrated in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 5</a>. PW defines the pulsewidth of the data symbols sent by the reader. The <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm TRcal}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-38-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-38">{\rm TRcal}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> interval is approximated by the number of clock cycles <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">N_{\rm Tag}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-39-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-39">N_{\rm Tag}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> whose duration is given by the oscillator frequency. Within this setup, the oscillator frequency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{\rm Tag}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-40-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-40">f_{\rm Tag}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is about 2.2 MHz, which relates to a clock interval <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">T_{\rm Tag}=454.5\ {\hbox {ns}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-41-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-41">T_{\rm Tag}=454.5\ {\hbox {ns}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The introduced relative frequency error is determined by <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">({\rm TRcal}-N_{\rm Tag}\cdot T_{\rm Tag})/{\rm TRcal}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-42-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-42">({\rm TRcal}-N_{\rm Tag}\cdot T_{\rm Tag})/{\rm TRcal}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Therefore, the higher the oscillation frequency, the less the relative error. However, the maximum frequency value is limited by the current consumption in the tag. For a deeper explanation of these parameters, refer to <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_2">[7]</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-5-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-5-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 5. </b><fig><p>Measurement of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm TRcal}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-43-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-43">{\rm TRcal}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5688469/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 6. </b><fig><p>Common architectures of reference circuits <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref35" id="context_ref_35_2">[35]</a>. (a) Voltage mode. (b) Current mode. (c) Current voltage mode.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5688469/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
The clock divider is used for enabling a continuous modulation with the modulation frequency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{\rm Mod}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-44-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-44">f_{\rm Mod}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. It is necessary for distance measurements with the technique of modulated backscattering, as explained in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_2">[14]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref33" id="context_ref_33_2">[33]</a>. The clock divider is designed as an asynchronous divider, as shown in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref33" id="context_ref_33_2">[33]</a>, with optimized logic cells of the process. The clock divider is only necessary for generating the modulation signal so it will be deactivated for other transponder functionalities to save power consumption.<p></p><p>Using a separate value of the modulation frequency for different transponders enables a distinction between them. An additional counter in the transponder circuit only for generating the modulation signal would offer the derivation of individual values for the modulation frequency, but would also increase the whole power consumption by some amount. Within this first test setup, only a fixed modulation frequency using a clock divider was implemented.</p><p>The maximum reading range depends essentially on two factors: first, the transponder needs a sufficient amount of energy for proper operation and a good efficient antenna. Second, there must be sufficient signal-to-noise ratio (SNR) available to read the transmitted data of the tag by the reader. When designing a purely passive transponder, the whole subcircuit is allowed to consume only few <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mu{\hbox {A}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-45-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-45">\mu{\hbox {A}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> to achieve a sufficiently high operating range. The circuit design must comply with low-power and low-voltage requirements. Varying supply voltages and temperatures are also unavoidable <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref20" id="context_ref_20_2">[20]</a>. By using active transponders with their own battery, represented by voltage source <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{\rm Aux}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-46-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-46">V_{\rm Aux}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 4</a>, a higher distance can be reached or a highly disturbed data transmission can be improved. Alternatively the transponder can also be used in a semipassive configuration in which the battery supply is only used for additional features like localization and sensing and the basic RFID functionality is still performed passively. For that operating case, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{\rm Aux}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-47-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-47">V_{\rm Aux}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can be connected to the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">VDD</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-48-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-48">VDD</script></tex-math></inline-formula> node using a power switch, which is enabled after receiving the related custom command for localization to hold the voltage at a constant level.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Description of the Single System Components</h2></div><p>This section evaluates possible architectures for the components that are candidates for both low-voltage and low-power requirements in the RFID chip. Furthermore, regarding low-cost applications the desired system parameters should be achieved without further tuning. According to these requirements, suitable architectures were investigated. Their performance and their drawbacks are compared.</p><div class="section_2" id="sec3a"><h3>A. Reference Circuit</h3><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 6</a> illustrates the general circuits possible to generate a reference voltage <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref35" id="context_ref_35_3a">[35]</a>. The voltage mode configuration [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 6(a)</a>] is based on the summation of a proportional to absolute temperature (PTAT) voltage with the complementary to absolute temperature (CTAT) voltage of a pn junction <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref36" id="context_ref_36_3a">[36]</a>. It is mostly implemented as a diode-connected bipolar transistor. The process used provides parasitic lateral bipolar devices, as presented in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref37" id="context_ref_37_3a">[37]</a>. Regarding RFID applications, this type of bandgap is not suitable because the supply voltage must be at least higher than the bandgap voltage of silicon (1.205 V at 27 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\ ^{\circ}{\hbox{C}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-49-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-49">\ ^{\circ}{\hbox{C}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) plus the saturation voltage of a MOS current source. Therefore, the minimum supply voltage would be around 1.5 V.</p><p>The current mode bandgap <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref38" id="context_ref_38_3a">[38]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref39" id="context_ref_39_3a">[39]</a> with the configuration of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 6(b)</a> is more suitable for this setup. The temperature characteristic of the bandgap has a curvature because the temperature dependence of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{\rm BE}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-50-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-50">V_{\rm BE}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> has a nonlinear term, which can be expressed by <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{T}\cdot\ln(T/T_{0})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-51-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-51">V_{T}\cdot\ln(T/T_{0})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">T_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-52-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-52">T_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the reference temperature <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref40" id="context_ref_40_3a">[40]</a>. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">I_{\rm NL}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-53-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-53">I_{\rm NL}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> describes a nonlinear current, which could compensate this nonlinear term. Besides the different bandgap structures, other circuit architectures were evaluated to be suitable for the desired requirements.</p><p>Recently reference circuits consisting of only MOS devices have attracted notice to designers. In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref41" id="context_ref_41_3a">[41]</a>, an equivalent design of the current mode bandgap <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref38" id="context_ref_38_3a">[38]</a> is shown using diode-connected pMOS transistors instead of pnp devices. They operate in weak inversion, where the exponential characteristics of bipolar transistors can be approximated. In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref42" id="context_ref_42_3a">[42]</a>, a CMOS reference utilizing subthreshold characteristics is also demonstrated, according to <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 6(b)</a>. In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref43" id="context_ref_43_3a">[43]</a>, an MOS circuit according to architecture <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 6(a)</a> is shown. The variations of the reference voltage due to supply voltage, temperature, and process variations have noticeably lower performance compared to the current mode bandgap.</p><p>However, despite its worse characteristics, the design concept of <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref43" id="context_ref_43_3a">[43]</a> was further investigated in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref44" id="context_ref_44_3a">[44]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref45" id="context_ref_45_3a">[45]</a> because of its very low power consumption, which is lower than bandgap references (with a reasonable dimensioning). There the process deviations were partially compensated with a decoder.</p><p>Finally, the architecture of the current mode bandgap <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref38" id="context_ref_38_3a">[38]</a> was selected as a common reference cell for both reference voltages and bias currents. An actual implementation of it is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 7</a> for convenience. The generation of two different bias currents using different division ratios of the pMOS current sources is demonstrated exemplarily.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 7. </b><fig><p>Architecture of the current mode bandgap.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5688469/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The reference voltage <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{\rm Ref}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-54-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-54">V_{\rm Ref}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the current mode bandgap is given by <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref38" id="context_ref_38_3a">[38]</a> <disp-formula id="deqn2" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{\rm Ref}={R_{3}\over R_{2}}\cdot\left[{R_{2}\ln M\over R_{1}}\cdot V_{T}+V_{\rm BE}\right] \eqno{\hbox{(2)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-55-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-55">V_{\rm Ref}={R_{3}\over R_{2}}\cdot\left[{R_{2}\ln M\over R_{1}}\cdot V_{T}+V_{\rm BE}\right] \eqno{\hbox{(2)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">V_{\rm Ref}={R_{3}\over R_{2}}\cdot\left[{R_{2}\ln M\over R_{1}}\cdot V_{T}+V_{\rm BE}\right] \eqno{\hbox{(2)}}</span></span></disp-formula>where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{T}=k\cdot T/q</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-56-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-56">V_{T}=k\cdot T/q</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-57-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-57">M</script></tex-math></inline-formula> denotes the number of parallel pnp devices <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Q_{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-58-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-58">Q_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 7</a>.</p><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-8-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-8-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 8. </b><fig><p>Adaption of the temperature curve.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5688469/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
The main focus for this low-power circuit design is to fulfill the requirements of the EPC protocol, which specifies temperatures up to 65 Â°C <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_3a">[7]</a>. There is no explicit requirement for the reference voltage, but there is an implicit one for the bias current <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">I_{\rm Bias2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-59-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-59">I_{\rm Bias2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 4</a>, which, in turn, influences the oscillator frequency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{\rm Tag}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-60-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-60">f_{\rm Tag}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.<p></p><p>However, wireless sensor networks in industrial environments can also be suitable for higher ambient temperatures than 65 Â°C demanding that the reference voltage must stay within a certain range. By adapting the temperature dependence to achieve a flat curve around ambient temperature, its slope increases for higher temperatures. In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref40" id="context_ref_40_3a">[40]</a>, a curvature compensation technique is presented. Unfortunately, using the available lateral pnp device <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref37" id="context_ref_37_3a">[37]</a> with its related temperature characteristics is not possible to parametrize the related resistors <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{4}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-61-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-61">R_{4}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{5}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-62-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-62">R_{5}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> shown in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref40" id="context_ref_40_3a">[40]</a> for compensating the nonlinear term in that way they have the same temperature dependence as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{\rm NL}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-63-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-63">V_{\rm NL}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. In fact, the curvature of the temperature curve increases. Another possibility is to increase the number <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-64-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-64">M</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of parallel bipolar transistors to achieve a more flat temperature curve. This procedure is illustrated in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 8</a>. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta V_{1}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-65-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-65">\Delta V_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta V_{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-66-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-66">\Delta V_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> represent the respective maximum deviations of the reference voltage for two intended temperature ranges. In configuration 2, the absolute deviation of the temperature curve caused by curvature between the boundary temperatures Â°C was evaluated; in configuration 1, it was increased up to 140 Â°C. Only those values of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-67-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-67">M</script></tex-math></inline-formula> should be used for the diode-connected bipolar transistors, which lead to a common centroid layout, as illustrated in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 9</a>, to achieve sufficient matching. The single pnp device in position 0 in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 9</a> (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Q_{1}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-68-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-68">Q_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 7</a>) is arranged in the middle. The parallel ones 1 to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-69-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-69">M</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are surrounded by it. According to the mentioned design constraints, the bandgap circuit was designed to have a power consumption of about 1 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\ \mu{\hbox {A}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-70-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-70">\ \mu{\hbox {A}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref37" id="context_ref_37_3a">[37]</a>. A fixed value of 4 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{{\hbox{M}}}\Omega</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-71-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-71">{{\hbox{M}}}\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> was selected for the resistor <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-72-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-72">R_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 7</a>. The adaption was achieved by resistor <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{1}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-73-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-73">R_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. To make a comparable evaluation, the same current sources P1âP3 were selected for all values of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-74-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-74">M</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, as originally designed for a configuration with eight parallel pnp devices <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Q_{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-75-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-75">Q_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Only the resistors <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{1}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-76-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-76">R_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for the temperature compensation and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{3}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-77-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-77">R_{3}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for the absolute value of the reference value were adapted. <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">TableÂ I</a> shows the results for different numbers <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-78-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-78">M</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of parallel pnp transistors.
