However, both the method of <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref40" id="context_ref_40_3a">[40]</a> and a higher number of parallel bipolar devices will, in principle, increase the whole current consumption of the bandgap.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig9"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-9-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-9-small.gif" alt="Figure 9" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 9. </b><fig><p>Common centroid layout of bipolar transistors in the bandgap.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5688469/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full table" id="table1"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">TableÂ I </b>Voltage Deviation Depending on Used Bipolar Transistors from Fig.Â 8<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-table-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-table-1-small.gif" alt="Table " /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<p></p><p>Using only eight parallel transistors <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Q_{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-79-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-79">Q_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the technique presented in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref37" id="context_ref_37_3a">[37]</a> can be used to reduce the curvature. By dimensioning the reference voltage <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{\rm Ref}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-80-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-80">V_{\rm Ref}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 7</a>, an internal bias current <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">I_{\rm Bias}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-81-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-81">I_{\rm Bias}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is generated <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref37" id="context_ref_37_3a">[37]</a>, which is temperature independent in first order without curvature compensation. Its absolute value depends on the size of the selected matching resistors. Fractional values of this current used for the other related cells in the transponder can be generated by respective ratios of the current mirror, as illustrated in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 7</a>. However, the temperature compensation scheme of <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref37" id="context_ref_37_3a">[37]</a> introduces the drawback that the bias current varies by some amount in the two compensation states of <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref37" id="context_ref_37_3a">[37]</a>. This is caused by the necessary different values of the resistors <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{1}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-82-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-82">R_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{3}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-83-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-83">R_{3}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. This, in turn, would influence the frequency value <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{\rm Tag}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-84-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-84">f_{\rm Tag}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the oscillator by some amount that is biased by it. It must be within the protocol requirements. Adding a second fractional bias current <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta I_{\rm Bias}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-85-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-85">\Delta I_{\rm Bias}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 10</a>, in the related state can relieve the situation if necessary. However, a large temperature change is not assumed during one communication cycle. The setting of the compensation state can be set fixed via the related control signal <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm Ctrl}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-86-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-86">{\rm Ctrl}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, as shown in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref33" id="context_ref_33_3a">[33]</a>, and can also be performed with a custom command.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig10"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-10-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-10-small.gif" alt="Figure 10" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 10. </b><fig><p>Adaption of bias current for different temperature compensation states.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5688469/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>Moreover the used resistors also have a certain temperature dependence. Regarding <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn2" href="#deqn2" class="fulltext-link">(2)</a>, the temperature dependence of the resistor ratios (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{3}/R_{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-87-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-87">R_{3}/R_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{2}/R_{1}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-88-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-88">R_{2}/R_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) can compensate each other. In the actual layout of the bandgap, the resistors <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{1}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-89-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-89">R_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{3}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-90-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-90">R_{3}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are separated in a greater number of unity resistors in series of about 45 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{{\hbox{k}}}\Omega</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-91-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-91">{{\hbox{k}}}\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, respectively, as illustrated in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 11</a>, with the related nodes of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 7</a>. These resistors were then matched to each other to diminish the process variations. The metal connection between the single resistors is arranged above and below them to improve matching. After the first layout design based on the simulated schematic, a fine tuning of the temperature matching was performed by using several unity resistors in parallel. Shorted dummy resistors are used on both ends of the resistor block to enable equal manufacturing conditions for all resistors <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref46" id="context_ref_46_3a">[46]</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig11"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-11-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-11-small.gif" alt="Figure 11" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 11. </b><fig><p>Concept of resistor matching for the bandgap.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5688469/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>Nevertheless, the reference circuit is only an auxiliary component for other circuits. Therefore, there does not exist an explicit demand by the EPC protocol for the accuracy of the reference voltage and of the bias current. It must only be guaranteed that the dependent components can achieve the defined performance. The bias current is used for the oscillator, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 4</a>. Wireless sensing is only an optional feature beyond the scope of the EPC protocol. The accuracy of the reference voltage only limits the possible resolution of the digitization.</p><p>The selection of its absolute value is twofold: on the one hand, it should be as high as possible to achieve a sufficient resolution for the digitization. On the other hand, it should be well below 1.0 V to enable a low supply voltage <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">VDD</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-92-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-92">VDD</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for the bandgap and a sufficient drainâsource voltage drop at the output transistor P3 of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 7</a>. As a first starting point of optimization, a value of 700 mV was selected. <a ref-type="table" anchor="table2" class="fulltext-link">TableÂ II</a> shows the step size using that reference voltage for different bit numbers of an ADC. For typical applications, the resolution should be at least 8 bits to achieve sufficient accuracy. The dynamic variations of the reference voltage on supply voltage must be smaller than half least significant bit (LSB) size for the desired resolution of the ADC. According to measurements shown in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref37" id="context_ref_37_3a">[37]</a>, the standard variation of the absolute value for the reference voltage is about <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sigma=11.2\ {{\hbox{mV}}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-93-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-93">\sigma=11.2\ {{\hbox{mV}}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. For achieving a good resolution of the ADC, the process variations are still too high. Therefore, the absolute value must be adapted after fabrication.
</p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table2"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">TableÂ II </b>Comparison of Different ADC Resolutions for a Reference Voltage <span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{\rm Ref}=700\ {{\hbox{mV}}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-94-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-94">V_{\rm Ref}=700\ {{\hbox{mV}}}</script><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-table-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-table-2-small.gif" alt="Table " /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3b"><h3>B. Startup Circuit</h3><p>Reference cells have two stable operating points. The task of the startup circuit is to ensure the right bias point after power up. The operating state with the intended reference voltage or bias current is the desired one. The other one leads to a zero cross current flow in the transistors of the reference cell. An external startup signal, which forces the circuit to the right point, shall be avoided because the circuit should ramp up by itself. Several startup circuits are discussed in the literature <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref35" id="context_ref_35_3b">[35]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref47" id="context_ref_47_3b">[47]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref48" id="context_ref_48_3b">[48]</a>.</p><p>The simplest implementation is using a capacitor, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 12</a>, without continuous cross current flow. During power-up, the capacitor <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-95-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-95">C_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is uncharged. Therefore, P8 is enabled and a transient drainâsource current can flow through it until <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-96-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-96">C_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is charged to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">VDD</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-97-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-97">VDD</script></tex-math></inline-formula> via P8, which then disables P9 and interrupts the startup current <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">I_{\rm Startup}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-98-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-98">I_{\rm Startup}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Alternatively, the gate of P8 can be held at a higher voltage level than directly connected to ground illustrated by the dashed voltage source <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V1</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-99-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-99">V1</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and the peak value of the drainâsource current in P8 is limited. This offers two advantages: firstly, the powering up is delayed to provide a reliable startup, and secondly, high cross currents that can stress the chip are avoided.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig12"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-12-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-12-small.gif" alt="Figure 12" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 12. </b><fig><p>Startup circuit with capacitor.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5688469/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>Regarding RFID systems, another boundary condition must be considered. After exceeding the minimal possible supply voltage <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">VDD</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-100-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-100">VDD</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and starting normal operation, the voltage level can decrease again under this value. In this situation, the whole circuit must restart reliably. However, if the supply voltage falls again, the capacitor <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-101-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-101">C_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is still loaded so a new startup current cannot flow yet. Only its leakage current can bring the capacitor back to its initial state. Therefore, it depends only on the bias cell which stable bias point to enter.</p><p>A startup circuit as shown in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref33" id="context_ref_33_3b">[33]</a> was implemented in the design. It is demonstrated in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig13" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 13</a>. At the output of the related inverter N6/P14 of <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref33" id="context_ref_33_3b">[33]</a>, an inverter was added to generate an inverted indication signal <i>Ref_ok</i> as a control signal for a power-on reset circuit. It turns to a logical LOW state after reaching steady state. It can be used to reset the digital part after powering up or disable the functionality of analog components during, for example, the transient interval.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig13"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-13-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-13-small.gif" alt="Figure 13" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 13. </b><fig><p>Implemented startup circuit <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref33" id="context_ref_33_3b">[33]</a>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5688469/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3c"><h3>C. Internal Clock Generator</h3><p>Oscillators of modern RF communication systems are usually embedded in a PLL as a VCO where its frequency value is adjusted by a high precision quartz oscillator. For RFID transponders, this solution is not suitable because quartz oscillators cannot be integrated on the transponder chip. In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref49" id="context_ref_49_3c">[49]</a>, a low-power remote frequency calibration method for passive UHF transponders is presented. The frequency value is adapted by an injection-locked phase-locked loop (IL-PLL). The calibrating RF signal is transmitted by the related reader. In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref50" id="context_ref_50_3c">[50]</a>, a similar method is presented. Here the reader sends several calibration signals with a predefined duration and a counter in the transponder chip compares them with the oscillation signal. The frequency value of the transponder is then adapted using the output settings of a successive approximation register (SAR).</p><p>The additional implementation of a calibration technique increases the power consumption of the transponder chip by some amount. The EPC protocol demands only a frequency accuracy of Â±2.5% during backscattering <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_3c">[7]</a>. If the related oscillator architecture can fulfill these requirements, this component can be integrated as a free-running oscillator. The oscillator itself is usually implemented as an <i>LC</i> tank oscillator. Regarding low-cost processes for high-volume applications that do not support the use of inductors, the family of relaxation oscillators was evaluated. Although they offer worse characteristics, they should be sufficient for RFID.</p><p>An oscillator involves no constant current consumption <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref51" id="context_ref_51_3c">[51]</a>. Depending on the actual loading state, its load current waveform has a different shape. The load capacitance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{\rm Buffer}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-102-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-102">C_{\rm Buffer}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 2</a> (or <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{\rm Osc}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-103-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-103">C_{\rm Osc}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 4</a> when using a regulator stage) must assure that the supply voltage is sufficiently constant to prevent influence and modulation.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 14</a> shows the common architectures of ring oscillators. They consist of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">N</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-104-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-104">N</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (odd) inverter stages and a delay circuit between them to define the frequency value. Every stage can be designed single-ended [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 14(a)</a>] or differentially [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 14(b)</a>]. In the simplest case, they can be realized by a CMOS inverter [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 14(c)</a>] or a single-stage differential amplifier with a differential output [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 14(d)</a>], respectively. A differential approach has the advantage to suppress common-mode disturbances. Simulations have shown their functionality with these differential amplifiers in principle. However, this implementation of one stage would actually need a common-mode feedback circuit <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref35" id="context_ref_35_3c">[35]</a> because there is no defined bias point at the output nodes of the differential amplifier. Depending on whether the transistors of the nMOS input amplifier or of the pMOS current mirror have more strength, the bias point at the output will increase or decrease. Therefore, every stage would need its own compensation circuit, which would increase the whole current consumption. Therefore, only the single-stage inverter chains are evaluated.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig14"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-14-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-14-small.gif" alt="Figure 14" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 14. </b><fig><p>Implementation of ring oscillators. (a) Single ended. (b) Differential. (c) Basic single-ended stage. (d) Basic differential stage.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5688469/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>In the single-ended stage, the current sources <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm IBias1}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-105-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-105">{\rm IBias1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm IBias2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-106-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-106">{\rm IBias2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can be implemented. Besides the load capacitor <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{5}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-107-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-107">C_{5}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the limited loading current can then also be used to define the frequency value. The necessary capacitor size of the stage and the whole current consumption of the oscillator can be decreased. Moreover, the cross current of the inverter is also reduced. The length <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">L</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-108-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-108">L</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the CMOS transistors should be several times larger than the minimum value for achieving sufficient matching. By increasing the width <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">W</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-109-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-109">W</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the cross current can be increased, but this also increases the related gate capacitance. It must be rather smaller than the desired load capacitance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{5}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-110-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-110">C_{5}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the delay element in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 14</a>, which determines the frequency value of the ring oscillator. Simulations of single-ended ring oscillators in the process used have shown worse characteristics depending on temperature and supply voltage.</p><p>Another implementation of relaxation oscillators is the cross-coupled <i>RC</i> multivibrator. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig15" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 15</a> shows its architecture. Its frequency value <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{RC}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-111-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-111">f_{RC}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is determined by <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref52" id="context_ref_52_3c">[52]</a> <disp-formula id="deqn3" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{RC}={I_{0}\over 2\cdot\Delta V_{AB}\cdot C_{M}} \eqno{\hbox{(3)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-112-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-112">f_{RC}={I_{0}\over 2\cdot\Delta V_{AB}\cdot C_{M}} \eqno{\hbox{(3)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">f_{RC}={I_{0}\over 2\cdot\Delta V_{AB}\cdot C_{M}} \eqno{\hbox{(3)}}</span></span></disp-formula>where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">I_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-113-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-113">I_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the respective cross current in the bias paths and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta V_{AB}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-114-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-114">\Delta V_{AB}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the voltage swing at the capacitor <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{M}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-115-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-115">C_{M}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Regarding the frequency determining time constant <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{4}\cdot C_{M}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-116-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-116">R_{4}\cdot C_{M}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the following parameters can be set. The current consumption should be as low as possible so the two resistors <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{4}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-117-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-117">R_{4}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are chosen to be several hundred <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\hbox{k}}\Omega</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-118-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-118">{\hbox{k}}\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{M}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-119-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-119">C_{M}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> as low as possible, but also being sufficiently above the order of parasitic capacitances in the final layout. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{4}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-120-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-120">R_{4}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> also defines the swing <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta V_{AB}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-121-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-121">\Delta V_{AB}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the signal. Ideally the mirrored bias current <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">I_{\rm Bias2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-122-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-122">I_{\rm Bias2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> only influences the magnitude of the oscillation swing and the steepness of the falling slope by decharging the capacitor <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{M}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-123-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-123">C_{M}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig15"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-15-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-15-small.gif" alt="Figure 15" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 15. </b><fig><p>Architecture of the <i>RC</i> oscillator.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5688469/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig16" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 16</a> illustrates the layout of the oscillator resistors <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{4}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-124-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-124">R_{4}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. They were arranged in a similar way as already shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 11</a>. The related nodes <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-125-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-125">C</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">D</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-126-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-126">D</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig15" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 15</a> are connected in the middle of the layout. Each of the two resistors are separated in several small resistors and arranged alternatively on the right and left side to achieve symmetry to the middle axis. The supply ports to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">VDD</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-127-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-127">VDD</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are connected at the outer left and right side.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig16"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-16-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-16-small.gif" alt="Figure 16" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 16. </b><fig><p>Concept of resistor matching for the <i>RC</i> oscillator.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5688469/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p><i>RC</i> oscillators need a capacitor for setting the frequency value. For this transponder setup, the desired frequency value should be around 2.2 MHz. MOS capacitances are nonlinear <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref35" id="context_ref_35_3c">[35]</a> and not suitable for a precise design. In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref33" id="context_ref_33_3c">[33]</a> the whole capacitance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{M}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-128-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-128">C_{M}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> was achieved by two metalâinsulatorâmetal (MIM) capacitors that are arranged antiparallel to counteract the parasitic capacitance between the lower metal plate and the n well or the p substrate. The dielectric layer between the two plates with a higher <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\epsilon_{r}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-129-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-129">\epsilon_{r}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> value than <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{{\hbox{SiO}}}_{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-130-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-130">{{\hbox{SiO}}}_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> enables a low capacitance area on the chip. There, only a low value of twice 80 fF was used. Although working, in principle, the measurement has shown a deviation of several hundred kilohertz of the oscillation frequency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{\rm Tag}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-131-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-131">f_{\rm Tag}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in comparison to the intended simulated value.</p><p>Avoiding a too high deviation by such a small capacitor, here a novel approach with matched metalâmetal (MM) capacitors was investigated. Due to the larger chip area, the related relative error <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta C/C_{M}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-132-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-132">\Delta C/C_{M}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> should be smaller. Furthermore, the capacitance value was slightly increased to overall 200 fF. In the actual process, basic MM capacitors can be used in all supported four metal layers of the layout. However, these layers are more close to the substrate and n well, which increases the parasitic capacitances. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig17" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 17(a)</a> shows the common architecture of an MM capacitance including the respective parasitic capacitances <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{\rm par}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-133-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-133">C_{\rm par}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. To achieve a high degree of symmetry, the whole capacitor was separated in four parallel capacitances on metal layers 2 to 4, respectively, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig17" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 17(b)</a>. They are connected to the related nodes of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig15" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 15</a> <disp-formula id="" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{M}=C_{1,M34}+C_{2,M23}+C_{3,M34}+C_{4,M23}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-134-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-134">C_{M}=C_{1,M34}+C_{2,M23}+C_{3,M34}+C_{4,M23}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">C_{M}=C_{1,M34}+C_{2,M23}+C_{3,M34}+C_{4,M23}</span></span></disp-formula>in <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn3" href="#deqn3" class="fulltext-link">(3)</a> is the parallel circuit of the four matched MM capacitors. The related layout is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig17" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 17(c)</a>. Metal layer 3 is used as one plate for all four capacitances. Metal layer 1 and 5 are used for shielding and are connected to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">VSS</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-135-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-135">VSS</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. In the alternative design with MIM capacitors in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref33" id="context_ref_33_3c">[33]</a>, only the parasitic capacitance of the lower plate was accounted for because this type is arranged at a higher metal layer. Therefore, matching with only two antiparallel capacitors was performed. <a ref-type="table" anchor="table3" class="fulltext-link">TableÂ III</a> shows a comparison between the two evaluated design approaches.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig17"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-17-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-17-small.gif" alt="Figure 17" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 17. </b><fig><p>Concept of capacitor matching for the <i>RC</i> oscillator.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5688469/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full table" id="table3"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">TableÂ III </b>Chip Size of Integrated Capacitors<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-table-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-table-3-small.gif" alt="Table " /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<p></p><p>The power switch <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm TGOsc}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-136-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-136">{\rm TGOsc}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for disabling the reference oscillator is inserted in the bias current path of the oscillator, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig15" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 15</a>. A switch in the supply rail would also avoid leakage by the related transistors of the oscillator circuit, but the channel width of the transistor switch has to be designed much wider to minimize the voltage drop caused by current flow. The used bias current <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">I_{\rm Bias2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-137-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-137">I_{\rm Bias2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig15" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 15</a> is only 100 nA in comparison to the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">VDD</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-138-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-138">VDD</script></tex-math></inline-formula> rail with an average current of about 1.5 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mu{\hbox {A}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-139-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-139">\mu{\hbox {A}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in the new design, and the current peaks during switching are several times higher depending on the size of the load capacitance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{\rm Buffer}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-140-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-140">C_{\rm Buffer}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> or <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{\rm Osc}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-141-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-141">C_{\rm Osc}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">VDD</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-142-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-142">VDD</script></tex-math></inline-formula> rail. Special high threshold voltage transistors have been used for the transfer gate. The threshold voltage of this device is set to a higher value by a higher channel doping concentration. This results in lower leakage and reliable isolation at high temperatures.</p><p>Further oscillator architectures suitable for RFID are shown in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref53" id="context_ref_53_3c">[53]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref54" id="context_ref_54_3c">[54]</a>.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3d"><h3>D. Voltage Regulator</h3><p>In the whole architecture according to <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Figs.Â 2</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">4</a>, the absolute frequency value of the reference oscillator is mainly influenced by two sources (except for process variations): the first one are slow variations of the supply voltage caused by changes in the air interface (distance, polarization), but with a large dynamic range. The second one are changes of the supply voltage caused by rectification, the activity of the backscatter modulator or in the case of localization its continuous modulation <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref32" id="context_ref_32_3d">[32]</a>. They usually have a small magnitude. Both effects will tune the oscillator frequency to some amount. The whole variation must be within the allowed range of the EPC protocol <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_3d">[7]</a>.</p><p>The second effect can be diminished by increasing the value of the load capacitance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{\rm Buffer}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-143-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-143">C_{\rm Buffer}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 2</a>, as yet to be illustrated in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec5" class="fulltext-link">SectionÂ V</a>. The first effect can be diminished additionally by the implementation of a low-voltage regulator. In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref32" id="context_ref_32_3d">[32]</a>, a low drop-out regulator using active resistances is presented. Due to the slow variation, its error amplifier need not to be fast. Therefore, the additional power consumption is only increased slightly. However, this would increase the minimal possible supply voltage. Using a voltage regulator, the related load capacitance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{\rm Osc}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-144-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-144">C_{\rm Osc}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at its output stabilizes the supply voltage, as depicted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 4</a>. Disclaiming a regulator, the overall load capacitance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{\rm Buffer}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-145-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-145">C_{\rm Buffer}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at the output of the rectifier must perform this task. In both cases, the actual value is a tradeoff between available power during backscattering, magnitude of the induced ripple, and the necessary chip area.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3e"><h3>E. Selection</h3><p>For comparing the performance of the different single components in the previous sections, two system concepts were evaluated. The first test chip consists of the modified current mode bandgap presented in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref37" id="context_ref_37_3e">[37]</a> combined with the novel <i>RC</i> oscillator with MM capacitors (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig15" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 15</a>) including a Modulo-8 clock divider <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref33" id="context_ref_33_3e">[33]</a> for testing the continuous modulation for distance measurement. The second one also includes the low-power voltage regulator of <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref32" id="context_ref_32_3e">[32]</a> with active devices providing a stabilized supply voltage <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{\rm Reg}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-146-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-146">V_{\rm Reg}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for the oscillator. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig18" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 18</a> shows the layout of the second test chip (the other one is just without the regulator). The resistors of the bandgap consume most of the chip area, but this is necessary to a achieve a sufficiently small current consumption.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig18"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-18-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-18-small.gif" alt="Figure 18" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 18. </b><fig><p>Layout of the second test chip.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5688469/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig19"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-19-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-19-small.gif" alt="Figure 19" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 19. </b><fig><p>Measurement setup for the transponder subcomponents.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5688469/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>

<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Measurement Setup for Reference Cells</h2></div><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig19" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 19</a> shows the measurement setup for the two test chips mentioned in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3e" class="fulltext-link">SectionÂ III-E</a>. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V1</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-147-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-147">V1</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the voltage supply (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">VDD</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-148-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-148">VDD</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) of the whole chip. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V2</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-149-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-149">V2</script></tex-math></inline-formula> denotes a supply voltage (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">VDD</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-150-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-150">VDD</script></tex-math></inline-formula>_2) for the ESD structures and the output buffers of the clock pads. With the current meter 1 their current consumption is evaluated. The voltage reference and the bias current are measured by voltmeter 1 and current meter 2, respectively. The frequency of the two clock signals <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm CLK}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-151-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-151">{\rm CLK}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm CLK}8</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-152-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-152">{\rm CLK}8</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are measured with a spectrum analyzer. The control signal <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm Ref\_ok}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-153-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-153">{\rm Ref\_ok}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is evaluated at the oscilloscope. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V3</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-154-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-154">V3</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V4</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-155-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-155">V4</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are used for the digital control signals <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm Osc\_En}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-156-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-156">{\rm Osc\_En}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm Ctrl}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-157-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-157">{\rm Ctrl}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Their high state are held at the same value as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">VDD</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-158-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-158">VDD</script></tex-math></inline-formula> as would be in the final implementation. The whole measurement is controlled via a PC. The test chips are packaged and the temperature dependence is evaluated in a temperature chamber. In this setup, the bias current adaption of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 10</a> was not used.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig20"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-20-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-20-small.gif" alt="Figure 20" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 20. </b><fig><p>Intended qualitative behavior of the reference voltage <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref37" id="context_ref_37_4">[37]</a>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5688469/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig21"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-21-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-21-small.gif" alt="Figure 21" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 21. </b><fig><p>Reference voltage <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{\rm Ref}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-159-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-159">V_{\rm Ref}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (V). (a) Dependence on temperature <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">T</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-160-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-160">T</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">({VDD}=1.0\ {{\hbox{V}}})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-161-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-161">({VDD}=1.0\ {{\hbox{V}}})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. <p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig20" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 20</a> demonstrates the basic design idea for the adaption of the reference voltage depending on temperature, as presented in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref37" id="context_ref_37_4">[37]</a>. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig21" class="fulltext-link">Figs.Â 21</a>â<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig22" class="fulltext-link"></a><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig23" class="fulltext-link"></a><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig24" class="fulltext-link"></a><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig25" class="fulltext-link">25</a> show the measurement results for the different parameter values depending on temperature <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">T</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-164-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-164">T</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and supply voltage <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">VDD</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-165-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-165">VDD</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{VDD}=1\ {{\hbox{V}}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-166-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-166">{VDD}=1\ {{\hbox{V}}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{T}=25\ ^{\circ}{{\hbox{C}}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-167-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-167">{T}=25\ ^{\circ}{{\hbox{C}}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are defined as normal operating conditions, which are common values in a typical UHF RFID scenario. All measurements were performed for the two temperature compensation states by setting the control signal <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm Ctrl}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-168-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-168">{\rm Ctrl}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, as described in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3a" class="fulltext-link">SectionÂ III-A</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref37" id="context_ref_37_4">[37]</a>.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig21" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 21</a> shows the related measured characteristics of the reference voltage <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{\rm Ref}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-169-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-169">V_{\rm Ref}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Regarding the bandgap structure, the measured wafer run has shown a slight mismatch. The accuracy of the temperature compensation scheme for the reference voltage, as shown in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref37" id="context_ref_37_4">[37]</a>, could not be achieved, but the general functionality of this approach is verified. This mismatch does not influence the performance of the whole transponder.</p><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig22"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-22-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-22-small.gif" alt="Figure 22" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 22. </b><fig><p>Bias current <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">I_{\rm Bias}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-170-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-170">I_{\rm Bias}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. (a) Dependence on temperature <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">T</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-171-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-171">T</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">({VDD}=1.0\ {{\hbox{V}}})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-172-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-172">({VDD}=1.0\ {{\hbox{V}}})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. <div class="figure figure-full" id="fig23"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-23-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-23-small.gif" alt="Figure 23" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 23. </b><fig><p>Multivibrator frequency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{\rm Tag}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-175-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-175">f_{\rm Tag}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. (a) Dependence on temperature <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">T</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-176-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-176">T</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">({VDD}=1.0\ {{\hbox{V}}})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-177-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-177">({VDD}=1.0\ {{\hbox{V}}})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. (b) Dependence on supply voltage <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">VDD</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-178-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-178">VDD</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">({T}=25\ ^{\circ}{{\hbox{C}}})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-179-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-179">({T}=25\ ^{\circ}{{\hbox{C}}})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5688469/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig23" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 23</a> shows the frequency characteristics of the novel <i>RC</i> oscillator. The relative error for the frequency value is marked around the default value for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">VDD</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-180-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-180">VDD</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and temperature. As mentioned in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3c" class="fulltext-link">SectionÂ III-C</a>, the relative frequency variation must be lower than Â±2.5% for the short period of backscattering. The dependence on the supply voltage for the measured range [0.85 V, 1.50 V] in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig23" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 23(b)</a> is within the specification. Supply voltages above this range, which can damage the transponder circuit, are prevented by a voltage limiter <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref29" id="context_ref_29_4">[29]</a>. Supply voltages below this range are suppressed by a power-on reset circuit which activates the transponder only above a certain voltage level. The dependence on temperature within the nominal temperature range <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">({T}=[-25\ ^{\circ}{{\hbox{C}}},40\ ^{\circ}{{\hbox{C}}}])</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-181-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-181">({T}=[-25\ ^{\circ}{{\hbox{C}}},40\ ^{\circ}{{\hbox{C}}}])</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and the extended temperature range <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">({T}=[-40\ ^{\circ}{{\hbox{C}}},65\ ^{\circ}{{\hbox{C}}}])</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-182-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-182">({T}=[-40\ ^{\circ}{{\hbox{C}}},65\ ^{\circ}{{\hbox{C}}}])</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are compliant to the specification of the EPC protocol. The influence of the analog frontend will still slightly increase this value. If the requirements of the EPC protocol cannot be guaranteed, one has to use the subcomponent with the additional regulator stage. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig25" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 25</a> shows the related frequency variation by using the regulator.
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig24"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-24-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-24-small.gif" alt="Figure 24" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 24. </b><fig><p>Modulation frequency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{\rm Mod}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-183-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-183">f_{\rm Mod}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for modulated backscattering. (a) Dependence on temperature <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">T</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-184-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-184">T</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">({VDD}=1.0\ {{\hbox{V}}})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-185-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-185">({VDD}=1.0\ {{\hbox{V}}})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.
