<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig25"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-25-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-25-small.gif" alt="Figure 25" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 25. </b><fig><p>Multivibrator frequency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{\rm Tag,Reg}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-188-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-188">f_{\rm Tag,Reg}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> with regulator <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">({T}=25\ ^{\circ}{{\hbox{C}}})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-189-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-189">({T}=25\ ^{\circ}{{\hbox{C}}})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5688469/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full table" id="table4"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">TableÂ IV </b>Current Consumption <span class="MathJax_Preview">(\mu{\hbox {A}})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-190-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-190">(\mu{\hbox {A}})</script> of the Different Circuit Configurations <span class="MathJax_Preview">({VDD}=1.2\ {{\hbox{V}}})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-191-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-191">({VDD}=1.2\ {{\hbox{V}}})</script><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-table-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-table-4-small.gif" alt="Table " /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<p></p><p><a ref-type="table" anchor="table4" class="fulltext-link">TableÂ IV</a> illustrates the whole current consumption of the two designed components in different configurations (including one enabled bias current, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig19" class="fulltext-link">Figs.Â 19</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig22" class="fulltext-link">22</a>). With the oscilloscope, a jitter analysis of the reference oscillator signal was performed using high-impedance probes. The test chip without regulator was evaluated with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\hbox{2}}\cdot {\hbox{10}}^{6}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-192-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-192">{\hbox{2}}\cdot {\hbox{10}}^{6}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> measurements (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{T}=25\ ^{\circ}{{\hbox{C}}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-193-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-193">{T}=25\ ^{\circ}{{\hbox{C}}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{VDD}=1.0\ {{\hbox{V}}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-194-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-194">{VDD}=1.0\ {{\hbox{V}}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>). A mean frequency of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\overline{f}_{\rm Tag}=2.1982\ {\hbox {MHz}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-195-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-195">\overline{f}_{\rm Tag}=2.1982\ {\hbox {MHz}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> with a standard deviation of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sigma=14.4998\ {\hbox {kHz}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-196-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-196">\sigma=14.4998\ {\hbox {kHz}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> was measured. The resulting <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3\cdot\sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-197-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-197">3\cdot\sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula> interval leads to an absolute frequency error of 2.1982 MHz Â± 43.4994 kHz. Therefore, the subcomponent fulfills the requirements of the EPC protocol (allowed 2.5% deviation equals 54.955 kHz).</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig26" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 26</a> shows the waveform of the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm Ref\_ok}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-198-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-198">{\rm Ref\_ok}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> signal at the startup circuit of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig13" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 13</a>. The test chip without a regulator was used under the denoted conditions. After enabling the supply voltage <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">VDD</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-199-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-199">VDD</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the startup circuit initiates the operation of the chip and the signal turns to the high state. After reaching the steady state, the startup circuit switches off and the output turns to low state. The actual shape of the waveform will be influenced by the available power at the RF port of the transponder chip and the implemented buffer capacitances <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{\rm Buffer}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-200-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-200">C_{\rm Buffer}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at the dc output of the rectifier stage, but the general functionality is verified. If the high state is too short, a capacitance can be added to delay the sequence.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig26"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-26-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-26-small.gif" alt="Figure 26" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 26. </b><fig><p>Waveform of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm Ref\_ok}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-201-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-201">{\rm Ref\_ok}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> signal (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{T}=25\ ^{\circ}{{\hbox{C}}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-202-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-202">{T}=25\ ^{\circ}{{\hbox{C}}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{VDD}=1\ {{\hbox{V}}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-203-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-203">{VDD}=1\ {{\hbox{V}}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>).</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5688469/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>Modulated Backscattering with Passive Transponders</h2></div><p>Many localization techniques are known in the literature <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref55" id="context_ref_55_5">[55]</a>. Unfortunately, because of the very limited power, most of them are not applicable for RFID. Within this setup, distance measurement is implemented using the basic frequency modulated continuous wave (FMCW) radar principle <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref56" id="context_ref_56_5">[56]</a> extended with the principle of modulated backscattering <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_5">[14]</a>. Here, the UHF transponder should perform continuous modulation during the distance measurement to clearly distinguish the transponder from undesired targets within the operating range of the FMCW reader. Here, modulated backscattering is implemented using the basic backscatter modulator of a UHF transponder (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 2</a>), as described in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_5">[14]</a>. The FMCW signal is placed in the ISM band of 2.45 GHz because here the allowed bandwidth is higher than in the UHF range <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_5">[14]</a>, as illustrated in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1</a>. The bandwidth influences the resolution and the peak width of the two peaks in the baseband spectrum of the FMCW reader, which are used for distance calculation <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_5">[15]</a>.</p><p>An alternative approach for implementing a distance measurement with the basic backscatter modulator and the EPC standard is shown in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref57" id="context_ref_57_5">[57]</a>. Here, the tag preamble or a user memory filled with zeros is used to generate the rectangular modulation signal for continuous modulation instead of deriving it from the transponder oscillator.</p><p>In the following, the whole application scenario with passive transponders and a continuous modulation is demonstrated. <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec5a" class="fulltext-link">SectionÂ V-A</a> shows theoretical limits for distance measurements with this two-frequency setup. <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec5b" class="fulltext-link">SectionÂ V-B</a> evaluates the influence on reference values during a continuous modulation. <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec5c" class="fulltext-link">SectionÂ V-C</a> shows distance measurements with the newly designed transponder consisting of the presented reference cells (<a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3e" class="fulltext-link">SectionÂ III-E</a>) and a novel multistandard antenna <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref58" id="context_ref_58_5">[58]</a>.</p><div class="section_2" id="sec5a"><h3>A. Theoretical Operating Range for Distance Measurement</h3><p>The basic functionality of modulated backscattering on the chip level with a complete RFID transponder for the UHF range in the process used is demonstrated in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_5a">[14]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_5a">[15]</a>. However, chip design is only one component of the whole transponder. The design of the necessary multistandard antenna will also influence the whole performance. Different antenna architectures are used depending on the desired whole tag size or on which material the tag is attached. An architecture as illustrated in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref58" id="context_ref_58_5a">[58]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref59" id="context_ref_59_5a">[59]</a> will be used. The adaption of the related transponder antenna for the input impedance of the current transponder chip is still in progress. Therefore, it makes sense to evaluate the theoretical power limitations of the actual transponder circuit first before attaching it to the antenna.</p><p>The free-air loss of effective power in the far field is determined by the Friis equation <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_5a">[11]</a>. In the far field, the electromagnetic wave has only a TEM mode, where the electric and magnetic field are perpendicular. Here, the border of the far field can be estimated with <disp-formula id="deqn4" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d_{\rm far}=2\cdot\lambda.\eqno{\hbox{(4)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-204-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-204">d_{\rm far}=2\cdot\lambda.\eqno{\hbox{(4)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">d_{\rm far}=2\cdot\lambda.\eqno{\hbox{(4)}}</span></span></disp-formula>Assuming far-field conditions, the free-air loss of the transmitted power <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{t}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-205-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-205">P_{t}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (one way) can be described by <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn5" href="#deqn5" class="fulltext-link">(5)</a> <disp-formula id="deqn5" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eqalignno{P_{t}=&amp;\,G_{t}\cdot\left({\lambda\over 4\pi d}\right)^{n}\cdot G_{r}\cdot P_{\rm Reader}\cr=&amp;\,G_{t}\cdot\left({\lambda\over 4\pi d}\right)^{n}\cdot D_{r}\cdot\eta_{r}\cdot P_{\rm Reader}\cr\geq&amp;\,G_{t}\cdot\left({\lambda\over 4\pi d}\right)^{n}\cdot D_{\rm Dipole}\cdot P_{\rm ERP}\cr=&amp;\,G_{t}\cdot\left({\lambda\over 4\pi d}\right)^{n}\cdot P_{\rm EIRP} &amp;\hbox{(5)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-206-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-206">\eqalignno{P_{t}=&amp;\,G_{t}\cdot\left({\lambda\over 4\pi d}\right)^{n}\cdot G_{r}\cdot P_{\rm Reader}\cr=&amp;\,G_{t}\cdot\left({\lambda\over 4\pi d}\right)^{n}\cdot D_{r}\cdot\eta_{r}\cdot P_{\rm Reader}\cr\geq&amp;\,G_{t}\cdot\left({\lambda\over 4\pi d}\right)^{n}\cdot D_{\rm Dipole}\cdot P_{\rm ERP}\cr=&amp;\,G_{t}\cdot\left({\lambda\over 4\pi d}\right)^{n}\cdot P_{\rm EIRP} &amp;\hbox{(5)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\eqalignno{P_{t}=&amp;\,G_{t}\cdot\left({\lambda\over 4\pi d}\right)^{n}\cdot G_{r}\cdot P_{\rm Reader}\cr=&amp;\,G_{t}\cdot\left({\lambda\over 4\pi d}\right)^{n}\cdot D_{r}\cdot\eta_{r}\cdot P_{\rm Reader}\cr\geq&amp;\,G_{t}\cdot\left({\lambda\over 4\pi d}\right)^{n}\cdot D_{\rm Dipole}\cdot P_{\rm ERP}\cr=&amp;\,G_{t}\cdot\left({\lambda\over 4\pi d}\right)^{n}\cdot P_{\rm EIRP} &amp;\hbox{(5)}}</span></span></disp-formula>where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm Reader}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-207-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-207">P_{\rm Reader}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the power of the reader, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">G_{t}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-208-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-208">G_{t}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the gain of the transponder antenna, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">G_{r}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-209-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-209">G_{r}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the gain of the reader antenna, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">D_{r}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-210-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-210">D_{r}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the directivity of the reader antenna, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta_{r}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-211-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-211">\eta_{r}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the efficiency of the reader antenna, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">D_{\rm Dipole}=1.64</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-212-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-212">D_{\rm Dipole}=1.64</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the directivity of a half-wave dipole, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\lambda=c/f</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-213-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-213">\lambda=c/f</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">n</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-214-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-214">n</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is a coefficient, which matches the propagation characteristics to different environmental conditions.</p><p>In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_5a">[3]</a>, the maximum allowed radiated power within a certain frequency range is mainly indicated as effective isotropic radiated power (EIRP) or equivalent radiated power (ERP). EIRP defines the power, which will radiate an idealized isotropic antenna <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(G_{r}=0\ {\hbox {dB}})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-215-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-215">(G_{r}=0\ {\hbox {dB}})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> to generate the same power density at the distance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-216-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-216">d</script></tex-math></inline-formula> as the antenna used <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(G_{r}&gt;0\ {\hbox {dB}})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-217-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-217">(G_{r}&gt;0\ {\hbox {dB}})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref23" id="context_ref_23_5a">[23]</a>. The power rating ERP is also widely used. In contrast to EIRP, ERP does not relate to an isotropic antenna, but to a half-wave dipole with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">D_{\rm Dipole}=1.64</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-218-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-218">D_{\rm Dipole}=1.64</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (2.15 dB). Therefore, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm EIRP}=1.64\cdot P_{\rm ERP}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-219-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-219">P_{\rm EIRP}=1.64\cdot P_{\rm ERP}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p><p>Regarding <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn5" href="#deqn5" class="fulltext-link">(5)</a>, the maximum operation range between reader and transponder can be influenced by the radiated power <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm Reader}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-220-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-220">P_{\rm Reader}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> or the gain of the reader antenna <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">G_{r}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-221-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-221">G_{r}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Reducing the radiated power (and increasing the gain) can reduce the power consumption of the reader. It also reduces the width of the main lobe, and therefore the influence of multipath effects. Against this, reducing the gain (and increasing the radiated power) increases the coverage area. This degree of freedom is not of concern for this examination so only <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm ERP}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-222-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-222">P_{\rm ERP}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> or <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm EIRP}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-223-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-223">P_{\rm EIRP}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are considered.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig27" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 27(a)</a> shows the related free-air loss of a transmitted signal at a certain distance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-224-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-224">d</script></tex-math></inline-formula> from the UHF reader (866 MHz) and the FMCW reader (2.45 GHz) (one-way propagation from the reader to the transponder). It is estimated using the basic Friis equation with the theoretical value of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">n=2</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-225-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-225">n=2</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and corresponds to the incident power <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{t}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-226-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-226">P_{t}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at the location of the transponder antenna. The gain of a basic dipole antenna for the transponder <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(G_{t}=2.15\ {\hbox {dB}})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-227-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-227">(G_{t}=2.15\ {\hbox {dB}})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> was used. It shall illuminate the general order of the decrease, but the precise curve highly depends on the related environment. For this common evaluation, maximum power levels according to <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_5a">[3]</a> are assumed.
</p><ul style="list-style-type:disc"><li><p><inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm ERP}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-228-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-228">P_{\rm ERP}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">({\hbox{866}}\ {\hbox {MHz}})={\hbox{33}}\ {{\hbox{dBm}}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-229-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-229">({\hbox{866}}\ {\hbox {MHz}})={\hbox{33}}\ {{\hbox{dBm}}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (2 W); annex 11, RFID.</p></li><li><p><inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm EIRP}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-230-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-230">P_{\rm EIRP}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">({\hbox{2.45}}\ {{\hbox{GHz}}})={\hbox{10}}\ {{\hbox{dBm}}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-231-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-231">({\hbox{2.45}}\ {{\hbox{GHz}}})={\hbox{10}}\ {{\hbox{dBm}}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (10 mW); annex 1, nonspecific short-range devices.</p></li></ul>Depending on polarization, the gain of the transponder antenna and the matching a certain amount is available at the rectifier output (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 2</a>). In a real environment, the operating range can also vary due to multipath effects.
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig27"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-27-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-27-small.gif" alt="Figure 27" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 27. </b><fig><p>(a) Incident power <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{t}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-232-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-232">P_{t}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> caused by free-air loss at 866 MHz and 2.45 GHz. (b) Backscattered power <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{b}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-233-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-233">P_{b}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at 2.45 GHz.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5688469/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The backscattered power <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{b}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-234-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-234">P_{b}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can be determined by <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn6" href="#deqn6" class="fulltext-link">(6)</a> (two-way propagation from the reader to the transponder and back) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_5a">[11]</a> <disp-formula id="deqn6" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{b}=G_{r}\cdot G_{t}^{2}\cdot\left({\lambda\over 4\pi d}\right)^{2\cdot n}\cdot\vert\Gamma_{\rm Trans}\vert^{2}\cdot P_{\rm EIRP}.\eqno{\hbox{(6)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-235-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-235">P_{b}=G_{r}\cdot G_{t}^{2}\cdot\left({\lambda\over 4\pi d}\right)^{2\cdot n}\cdot\vert\Gamma_{\rm Trans}\vert^{2}\cdot P_{\rm EIRP}.\eqno{\hbox{(6)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">P_{b}=G_{r}\cdot G_{t}^{2}\cdot\left({\lambda\over 4\pi d}\right)^{2\cdot n}\cdot\vert\Gamma_{\rm Trans}\vert^{2}\cdot P_{\rm EIRP}.\eqno{\hbox{(6)}}</span></span></disp-formula> <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig27" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 27(b)</a> shows the maximum backscattered power at 2.45 GHz. Here, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">G_{t}=2.15\ {\hbox {dB}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-236-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-236">G_{t}=2.15\ {\hbox {dB}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and a maximum reflection <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Gamma_{\rm Trans}=1</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-237-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-237">\Gamma_{\rm Trans}=1</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at the transponder antenna was assumed. A commercial reader antenna with a gain of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">G_{r}=8.5\ {\hbox {dB}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-238-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-238">G_{r}=8.5\ {\hbox {dB}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> was used for simulation.</p><p>The maximum range of the distance measurement finally depends on the sensitivity of the FMCW reader. Neglecting other effects, the theoretical upper limitation for a given input power value can be estimated.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec5b"><h3>B. Influence on Reference Values by Modulated Backscattering</h3><p>Within this section, the influence on the reference values during backscattering shall be evaluated in more detail. The circuit of <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3e" class="fulltext-link">SectionÂ III-E</a> without a regulator stage was used for this evaluation. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig28" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 28</a> demonstrates the used simulation setup. For a basic evaluation, an RF power source was used that emulates the delivered power of the antenna (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 2</a>). In the simulation, it has the optimal antenna impedance (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">L_{\rm Opt}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-239-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-239">L_{\rm Opt}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{\rm Opt}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-240-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-240">R_{\rm Opt}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> including the matching network for power matching). This impedance must be provided only by the antenna or with respective matching according to <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 4</a>. The RF input impedance of the transponder chip is mainly given by the related analog frontend and the actual loading state at the output of the rectifier. An RF input power <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{t}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-241-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-241">P_{t}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> between values from â12 to â10 dBm were assumed. Higher power values are then actually partially mismatched and some part of the incident power would be reflected, but the net power would be enough to perform transponder functionality. The output node <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{\rm Mod}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-242-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-242">f_{\rm Mod}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the clock divider (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 4</a>) was connected to the control port <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm Mod\_in}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-243-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-243">{\rm Mod\_in}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the backscatter modulator (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 2</a>). In the setup, the digital input signals <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm Ctrl}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-244-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-244">{\rm Ctrl}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm Osc\_En}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-245-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-245">{\rm Osc\_En}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the reference cell were set to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">VDD</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-246-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-246">VDD</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The simulations were performed including the parasitics of the respective layouts.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig28"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-28-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-28-small.gif" alt="Figure 28" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 28. </b><fig><p>Simulation setup.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5688469/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The simulation is performed as follows. At the beginning, the dc voltage level <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">VDD</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-247-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-247">VDD</script></tex-math></inline-formula> increases by rectifying the RF input signal until reaching the steady state. The clock divider and the and gate are still disabled by the control source <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm CLK \ Enable}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-248-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-248">{\rm CLK \ Enable}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The related waveforms at the nodes <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">VDD</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-249-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-249">VDD</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{\rm Ref}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-250-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-250">V_{\rm Ref}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{\rm Tag}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-251-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-251">f_{\rm Tag}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are recorded in steady state for different values of the buffer capacitance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{\rm Buffer}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-252-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-252">C_{\rm Buffer}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The same procedure is then repeated with the activated control source <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm CLK \ Enable}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-253-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-253">{\rm CLK \ Enable}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> to investigate the influence of modulated backscattering on these nodes performed by the backscatter modulator. One can estimate how much the capacitor value must be that the frequency of the reference oscillator is within the specification of the EPC protocol.</p><p>It is not possible to simulate the whole transponder circuit including the digital part in appropriate time for all states. Here, a fixed load resistor <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{L}=100\ {{\hbox{k}}}\Omega</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-254-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-254">R_{L}=100\ {{\hbox{k}}}\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> emulates the average current consumption of the remaining transponder components. A dc current of at least 10 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mu{\hbox {A}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-255-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-255">\mu{\hbox {A}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> flows through <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{L}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-256-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-256">R_{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> to sustain the functionality of all other necessary components. This evaluation should only illustrate the general trend of the parameter dependence. It must be assumed that the level of power matching and the ideal antenna impedance can only be approximated with real antennas. Therefore, a higher bias current also during modulation was assumed.</p><p>The actual value of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{\rm Buffer}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-257-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-257">C_{\rm Buffer}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 4</a> in the whole scenario must be selected depending on a worst case evaluation. It is created by a related number <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">N</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-258-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-258">N</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of unity MOS capacitors with a size of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{W/L}=10\ \mu{\hbox {m}}/10\ \mu{\hbox {m}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-259-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-259">{W/L}=10\ \mu{\hbox {m}}/10\ \mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, respectively. Each of them provides a related capacitance of about 575 fF. Additionally, if the chip area above the MOS capacitors is unused, the metal layers can also be connected and increase the whole capacitor size by some amount (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig29" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 29</a>). Integrated capacitors can only be used economically up to some hundred picofarads. Higher values would be possible by attaching external lumped components, but this is undesired for low-cost applications.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig29"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-29-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-29-small.gif" alt="Figure 29" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 29. </b><fig><p>MOS and metal capacitors for dc output.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5688469/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>Actually, this continuous modulation must only be possible for the duration of the modulation interval <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">T</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-260-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-260">T</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the FMCW reader for a confident detection, as described in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref33" id="context_ref_33_5b">[33]</a>.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig30" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 30</a> shows the relative error for the different system parameters depending on the load capacitance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{\rm Buffer}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-261-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-261">C_{\rm Buffer}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> used without continuous modulation of the backscatter modulator <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">({\rm CLK \ Enable}=0)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-262-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-262">({\rm CLK \ Enable}=0)</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. They are normalized to their respective mean value.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig30"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-30-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-30-small.gif" alt="Figure 30" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 30. </b><fig><p>Relative error caused by rectification without continuous modulation. (a) Error on supply voltage <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta VDD/\overline{VDD}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-263-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-263">\Delta VDD/\overline{VDD}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. (b) Error on oscillator frequency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta f_{\rm Tag}/\overline{f_{\rm Tag}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-264-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-264">\Delta f_{\rm Tag}/\overline{f_{\rm Tag}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. (c) Error on reference voltage <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta V_{\rm Ref}/\overline{V_{\rm Ref}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-265-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-265">\Delta V_{\rm Ref}/\overline{V_{\rm Ref}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5688469/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig31" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 31</a> shows the equivalent values during backscattering <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">({\rm CLK \ Enable}=1)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-266-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-266">({\rm CLK \ Enable}=1)</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig31" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 31(b)</a> shows the variation of the frequency value. With this setup, at least about 250 unity capacitors are necessary to fulfill the requirements of the EPC protocol (allowed frequency variation Â±2.5% <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_5b">[7]</a>). In <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig31" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 31(c)</a>, one can see in evidence that the reference voltage has an unacceptable high deviation during continuous modulation, but this will be not important because no sensing is performed during backscattering. Otherwise a simple preregulator can be used, which improves the supply voltage waveform of the bandgap. However, this would increase power consumption and the minimal possible supply voltage. Moreover, all unnecessary circuit components can be deactivated during backscattering, thus the power consumption will further decrease <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(&lt;{\hbox{10}}\ \mu{\hbox {A}})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-267-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-267">(&lt;{\hbox{10}}\ \mu{\hbox {A}})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig31"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-31-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-31-small.gif" alt="Figure 31" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 31. </b><fig><p>Relative error caused by rectification with continuous modulation. (a) Error on supply voltage <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta VDD/\overline{VDD}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-268-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-268">\Delta VDD/\overline{VDD}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. (b) Error on oscillator frequency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta f_{\rm Tag}/\overline{f_{\rm Tag}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-269-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-269">\Delta f_{\rm Tag}/\overline{f_{\rm Tag}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. (c) Error on reference voltage <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta V_{\rm Ref}/\overline{V_{\rm Ref}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-270-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-270">\Delta V_{\rm Ref}/\overline{V_{\rm Ref}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5688469/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec5c"><h3>C. Measurement Setup for Distance Measurement</h3><p>Finally, the distance measurement using the technique of modulated backscattering was evaluated. The whole algorithm for the distance measurement works, as already described in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_5c">[15]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_5c">[16]</a>. In those publications, the performance of the transponder chip regarding modulated backscattering was evaluated successfully. Here, first free-air measurements with the transponder chip attached to the newly designed multistandard antenna <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref58" id="context_ref_58_5c">[58]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref59" id="context_ref_59_5c">[59]</a> are shown. The accuracy of the distance measurement depends on the available power of the transponder, the used transponder antenna and the used reflector <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_5c">[15]</a>.</p><p>Within this setup, the distance measurement is intended as an optional feature for passive low-cost transponders without the need of additional high-performance components for localization. By using the backscatter modulator of the passive transponder also for distance measurement, only a small extension in the digital part of the transponder circuit (clock divider, implementation of the related custom command) is necessary. It does not noticeably increase the whole power consumption and chip area. Here, the distance information can be used for comfort functionalities. In automotive applications, some functionalities of a car can be activated, e.g., when the related person is moving to it.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig32" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 32</a> shows the whole measurement setup for the distance measurement using this multifrequency RFID system. The two readers and the designed transponder are arranged on a positioning stage. The transponder chip includes all necessary components to be compliant to the EPC protocol. The performance of the used reference oscillator and the bias cell are described in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4" class="fulltext-link">SectionÂ IV</a>. Here, the configuration without the voltage regulator was used. The design of the implemented analog frontend is not subject of this evaluation and refers to <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref31" id="context_ref_31_5c">[31]</a>. The design of the digital part is described briefly in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_5c">[16]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref17" id="context_ref_17_5c">[17]</a>. Both reader antennas <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref60" id="context_ref_60_5c">[60]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref61" id="context_ref_61_5c">[61]</a> are attached close to each other.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig32"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-32-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-32-small.gif" alt="Figure 32" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 32. </b><fig><p>Distance measurement with whole RFID system.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5688469/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p><a ref-type="table" anchor="table5" class="fulltext-link">TableÂ V</a> illustrates how the custom command for the distance measurement âLocateâ is implemented in the digital part. The initial bit sequence 11100000 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(0xE0)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-271-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-271">(0xE0)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is fixed by the EPC protocol to recognize a transmitted command as a defined custom command <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_5c">[7]</a>. The following 4 bits determine the âLocateâ command <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(0xF)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-272-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-272">(0xF)</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The command parameter <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">X</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-273-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-273">X</script></tex-math></inline-formula> sets the intended duration of the continuous modulation <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_5c">[15]</a>. Within this setup, it can be adapted by the user from 0.6 ms <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(X=0b0000)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-274-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-274">(X=0b0000)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> to 1.4 ms <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(X=0b1111)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-275-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-275">(X=0b1111)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in 16 steps.
</p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table5"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">TableÂ V </b>User-Defined EPC Custom Command for Distance Measurement<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-table-5-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-table-5-small.gif" alt="Table " /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig33"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-33-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5730005/5688469/5688469-fig-33-small.gif" alt="Figure 33" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 33. </b><fig><p>(<i>top</i>) Mean distance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\overline{d}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-276-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-276">\overline{d}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. (<i>middle</i>) Standard deviation <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-277-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-277">\sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of distance. (<i>bottom</i>) Absolute error <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta d/\overline{d}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-278-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-278">\Delta d/\overline{d}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of distance calculation.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5688469/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>After the custom command for the distance measurement is sent by the UHF reader, the transponder performs a continuous modulation with its backscatter modulator. The distance measurement is then carried out with the FMCW reader. The algorithm of distance calculation is described in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_5c">[16]</a>. The reflection coefficient <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Gamma_{\rm Trans}(f)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-279-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-279">\Gamma_{\rm Trans}(f)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the transponder antenna has different values at 866 MHz and at 2.45 GHz. At UHF, most of the power shall be absorbed by the transponder chip to enable data communication with the UHF reader, while at 2.45 GHz most of the power shall be reflected back to the FMCW reader to increase the possible operating range for the distance measurement. Therefore, performing only a PSK modulation between the two modulation states of the backscatter modulator would be best at 2.45 GHz. The design of the antenna is described in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref58" id="context_ref_58_5c">[58]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref59" id="context_ref_59_5c">[59]</a>. The antenna structure is fabricated on a PCB substrate in the ID-1 format (85.60 mm Ã 53.98 mm) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref62" id="context_ref_62_5c">[62]</a>. Its impedance is sufficiently matched to the RF port of the transponder chip so a matching network was not used between the transponder antenna and the chip (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 2</a>).</p><p>The EPC code of our multistandard transponder could be read with a commercial reader setup <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref60" id="context_ref_60_5c">[60]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref63" id="context_ref_63_5c">[63]</a> up to about 6.5 m with a radiated power <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm EIRP}=29\ {{\hbox{dBm}}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-280-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-280">P_{\rm EIRP}=29\ {{\hbox{dBm}}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Unfortunately, commercial UHF readers cannot be used for the distance measurement because up to now the custom command option is still not implemented in any available readers. Therefore, a custom-made UHF reader based on an FPGA board was used on which the EPC protocol is programmed. It allows the convenient implementation of the user-defined custom command. Measurements have shown a lower sensitivity of the RF frontend included in the FPGA solution than the commercial setup. It leads to a limited detection range of about 2.0 m, but the comparative measurement with the commercial reader has shown an extended operating range of the transponder.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig33" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 33</a> demonstrates the measurement results with the RFID system. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\hbox{10}}^{3}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-281-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-281">{\hbox{10}}^{3}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> measurements were performed for every distance value. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig33" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 33</a> (top) shows the measured mean distance value <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\overline{d}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-282-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-282">\overline{d}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig33" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 33</a> (middle) shows the related standard deviation <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-283-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-283">\sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig33" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 33</a> (bottom) shows the absolute error <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta d/\overline{d}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-284-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-284">\Delta d/\overline{d}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec6"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION VI.</div><h2>Conclusion and Outlook</h2></div><p>This paper has shown different circuit components for the transponder design combining the requirements for distance measurement, sensing, and multistandard performance in one subcircuit. This final subcomponent was implemented in the newly designed transponder chip. The distance measurement with the complete transponder can be initiated compliant to the EPC protocol. Finally, the distance measurement with the whole transponder using the technique of modulated backscattering was verified.</p><p>However, the development of the whole RFID system is still not finished. A redesign of the customized UHF reader will increase the operating range of the system. Future work should also focus on optimization of the multistandard antenna. The first setup was mainly focused on the characteristics of the UHF range (866 MHz) where power matching is performed. Adapted modulation states of the transponder antenna at 2.45 GHz can achieve a more reliable distance measurement. Furthermore, a second backscatter modulator equipped with certain impedance values for achieving a better PSK modulation (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 3</a>) and only intended for modulating backscattering could also improve the setup. Better results are feasible with the use of an FMCW radar at a base frequency of 5.8 GHz providing a larger bandwidth (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1</a>).</p></div>
<h3>ACKNOWLEDGMENT</h3><p>The transponder was developed jointly at the Institute for Electronics Engineering, University of ErlangenâNuremberg, Nuremberg, Germany, the Institute of Radiofrequency and Microwave Engineering, Leibniz UniversitÃ¤t Hannover, Hannover, Germany, and the Infineon Design Center Graz, Graz, Germany, within the scope of a research project supported by the Bavarian Research Foundation <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref64" id="context_ref_64_">[64]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref65" id="context_ref_65_">[65]</a>. The layout of the transponder chip was processed in the fabs of Infineon. The FMCW reader hardware and the related software for signal processing were developed by Siemens CT, Munich, Germany.</p></div></div>

				<strong class="ng-binding">Author Keywords </strong>
				<div>
					<!-- ngRepeat: term in ::keyword.kwd track by $index --><span ng-repeat="term in ::keyword.kwd track by $index" class="ng-binding ng-scope">

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

	}
});

It is intended to be a common reference cell, both for basic UHF requirements and advanced application fields like local positioning and wireless sensing. Different single circuit topologies shown in previous studies or literature and their applicability for that RFID system are evaluated.
